# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Kubernetes Server-Side Apply Configuration Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a deep guide for applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply semantics, including conflict handling and workflow patterns.

## Scope

Focus on the applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

97-assistanttext-
The document has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

---

**Structure of the guide:**

1. **Purpose and Boundaries** — explains what SSA is (declarative field-ownership protocol), what it replaces (client-side three-way diff), and maps every layer from SMD up through the API server and client-go.

2. **Key Components and Responsibility Split** — walks the full `Manager` decorator chain assembled in `NewDefaultFieldManager` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:57-75`), with one row per layer explaining its single responsibility. Also covers `TypeConverter`, `ManagedInterface`, and the code-generated `ApplyConfiguration` builders.

3. **End-to-End Control Flow** — traces a request from the client building a `PodApplyConfiguration`, through `client-go/util/apply.NewRequest` setting the `Content-Type` header, through the `PatchResource` HTTP handler (`handlers/patch.go`), into the `FieldManager.Apply` decode-merge-encode cycle, down to `structuredMergeManager.Apply` calling SMD's `merge.Updater`, and back up through conflict surfacing as a `409 StatusError`.

4. **Failure Modes, Limits, and Tradeoffs** — covers conflict errors, version mismatches, the 10-manager cap and its `ancient-changes` buckets, schema-free CRDs forcing atomic list semantics, the `before-first-apply` bootstrap, `UpdateNoErrors` silent degradation, admission webhook interference, and scale subresource path remapping.

5. **Extension Points** — `TypeConverter` injection, `resetFields` filter, custom `Manager` wrappers, the `ForKind` dispatch, and the extract-modify-apply pattern with concrete code.

6. **Operational Implications** — TypeConverter startup cost, the noop-timestamp transformer and its performance impact, manager-entry accumulation from unstable names, 
... (truncated)

{
  "content": "# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and ApplyConfigurations: A Deep Guide\n\n## 1. Purpose and Boundaries\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative ownership protocol built into the Kubernetes API server. Where the older `kubectl apply` (client-side apply) computed a three-way diff on the client and then submitted a strategic-merge patch, SSA moves the merge logic entirely to the server. The server becomes the single source of truth about which actor controls each field of a resource, and conflicts between actors are surfaced as hard errors rather than silently clobbered.\n\nThe system has two main purposes:\n\n1. **Field ownership tracking** \u2013 every field in a resource's live state is attributed to the last manager that set it, stored in `metadata.managedFields`.\n2. **Controlled merge** \u2013 when a new apply is received the server merges the incoming \"desired intent\" with the live state under explicit conflict semantics: unknown fields that the caller does not touch are left alone; fields the caller explicitly declares ownership of that are already owned by a different manager produce a `409 Conflict` unless `force=true` is passed.\n\n### Upstream / downstream dependencies\n\n| Layer | What it provides |\n|---|---|\n| `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` (SMD) | Schema-aware value comparison, field-path representations, `merge.Updater` (the merge engine) |\n| `k8s.io/kube-openapi` | Converts OpenAPI v2 models into SMD schema types |\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields` | Public facade: `FieldManager`, `TypeConverter`, `ExtractInto`, `ScaleHandler`, `GvkParser` |\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal` | All business logic: the layered `Manager` chain, encoding/decoding, conflict formatting |\n| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers` | HTTP `PATCH` handler that selects SSA when `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml` (or `+cbor`) |\n| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager` | Admission controller wrapper (`managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController`), noop-timestamp optimization |\n| `k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations` | Code-generated, type-safe Go builders (one per API kind/version) for constructing apply payloads |\n| `k8s.io/client-go/util/apply` | Thin helper that marshals an apply configuration and sets the right `Content-Type` header |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 The `Manager` interface\n\n```\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/manager.go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n    Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, fieldManager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n}\n```\n\n`Manager` is the central abstraction. Every behavioural concern is implemented as a separate `Manager` wrapper that decorates an inner `Manager`. The production chain is assembled in `NewDefaultFieldManager` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:57-75`) as a nested sequence of constructors, innermost first:\n\n```\nVersionCheckManager\n  \u2514\u2500 LastAppliedUpdater\n       \u2514\u2500 LastAppliedManager\n            \u2514\u2500 ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager\n                 \u2514\u2500 CapManagersManager\n                      \u2514\u2500 BuildManagerInfoManager\n                           \u2514\u2500 ManagedFieldsUpdater\n                                \u2514\u2500 StripMetaManager\n                                     \u2514\u2500 structuredMergeManager   \u2190 SMD engine\n```\n\nEach layer has a single, narrow job:\n\n| Layer | File | Job |\n|---|---|---|\n| `structuredMergeManager` | `internal/structuredmerge.go` | Calls `merge.Updater.Update` / `.Apply`; owns all object-to-typed and typed-to-object conversions; applies defaults after a successful apply |\n| `StripMetaManager` | `internal/stripmeta.go` | Removes synthetic paths (`apiVersion`, `kind`, `metadata.name`, `metadata.managedFields`, \u2026) from the resulting field set so they are never tracked as owned |\n| `ManagedFieldsUpdater` | `internal/managedfieldsupdater.go` | For updates: detects whether any fields actually changed (by using a sentinel manager name `current-operation`) and, if so, merges them into the real manager entry and stamps the current time. For applies: stamps the operation time |\n| `BuildManagerInfoManager` | `internal/buildmanagerinfo.go` | Serialises the manager identifier: for updates it encodes `{manager, operation, apiVersion, subresource}` as JSON; for applies it omits `apiVersion` so a manager is always the same identity across versions |\n| `CapManagersManager` | `internal/capmanagers.go` | Caps the number of update-type manager entries at `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers` (10) by merging the oldest entries into per-version `ancient-changes` buckets |\n| `ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager` | `internal/skipnonapplied.go` | For objects with no managed fields, skips tracking on updates; for applies, synthesises an `Update` for the live object under the name `before-first-apply` so that the first apply has something to merge against |\n| `LastAppliedManager` | `internal/lastappliedmanager.go` | Intercepts `kubectl` applies and, if there are conflicts, checks whether the conflicting fields were previously owned by the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation; if so, auto-forces those specific fields (CSA\u2192SSA migration) |\n| `LastAppliedUpdater` | `internal/lastappliedupdater.go` | After a successful `kubectl` apply, keeps the `last-applied-configuration` annotation in sync with the new configuration (backward compatibility) |\n| `VersionCheckManager` | `internal/versioncheck.go` | Rejects applies whose `apiVersion/kind` do not match the request scope's GVK |\n\n### 2.2 `FieldManager` (public facade)\n\n`internal.FieldManager` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:45-48`) is not another `Manager` implementor in the chain; it is the outermost struct that callers interact with directly. It owns two responsibilities:\n\n1. Decoding the wire-format `metadata.managedFields` slice from `metav1.ManagedFieldsEntry` into the SMD-internal `fieldpath.ManagedFields` representation (`DecodeManagedFields`).\n2. Re-encoding the result back into `metadata.managedFields` after a successful operation (`EncodeObjectManagedFields`).\n\nThe public package exposes only a type alias (`type FieldManager = internal.FieldManager`) at `managedfields/fieldmanager.go:32` and two constructors:\n\n- `NewDefaultFieldManager` \u2013 for built-in typed API resources; requires a non-nil `TypeConverter` derived from the OpenAPI model.\n- `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` \u2013 for CRDs; uses `deducedTypeConverter` which treats all lists as atomic (no structural schema required).\n\n### 2.3 `TypeConverter`\n\n```\n// internal/typeconverter.go:34-37\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    ObjectToTyped(runtime.Object, ...typed.ValidationOptions) (*typed.TypedValue, error)\n    TypedToObject(*typed.TypedValue) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\nTwo implementations:\n\n- `typeConverter` (`internal/typeconverter.go:39-43`) \u2013 OpenAPI-backed; maps each GVK to a `*typed.ParseableType` built from `schemaconv.ToSchemaFromOpenAPI`. For unstructured objects it calls `t.FromUnstructured`; for structured it calls `t.FromStructured`.\n- `deducedTypeConverter` (`internal/typeconverter.go:75-100`) \u2013 schema-free; uses `typed.DeducedParseableType` which treats all lists atomically. Used for CRDs without structural schemas.\n- `schemeTypeConverter` (`internal/runtimetypeconverter.go`) \u2013 runtime-Scheme-backed; looks up the OpenAPI definition name from the Scheme (`scheme.ToOpenAPIDefinitionName`), then delegates to the parser. Introduced in 2025 as an alternative to the OpenAPI-map-based approach.\n\n### 2.4 `Managed` / `ManagedInterface`\n\n`fieldpath.ManagedFields` (from SMD) maps a JSON-encoded manager identifier string to a `fieldpath.VersionedSet` (a field set tagged with its API version and an `Applied` flag). The Kubernetes layer wraps this with timestamps in `managedStruct` implementing `ManagedInterface` (also aliased as `Managed`).\n\nManager identifiers are JSON-encoded `metav1.ManagedFieldsEntry` structs with `FieldsType`, `FieldsV1`, and `Time` zeroed out (see `BuildManagerIdentifier`, `internal/managedfields.go:134-158`). For applies, `APIVersion` is also omitted, making the identifier stable across version upgrades.\n\n### 2.5 ApplyConfiguration builders (client-go)\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` contains one auto-generated Go file per API type (e.g., `core/v1/pod.go`). Each file defines:\n\n- A `*ApplyConfiguration` struct with all fields as pointers (absent = not set, present = intent to set/own).\n- `With*` fluent builder methods for every field.\n- A `ForKind(gvk)` dispatch function in `utils.go` (1920-line generated file) that returns the correct zero-value `*ApplyConfiguration`.\n- `Extract*From` functions that call `managedfields.ExtractInto` to reconstruct the apply configuration from an existing live object's managed-fields entry \u2014 enabling the extract-modify-apply pattern.\n\n`ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration` (`meta/v1/objectmeta.go`) is the metadata half; it uses pointer fields to distinguish \"set this field\" from \"don't touch this field\", mirroring the JSON `omitempty` semantics that drive the SMD merge.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Client side\n\n1. The caller builds an `*ApplyConfiguration` (e.g., `corev1.Pod(\"my-pod\", \"default\").WithSpec(...)`) or extracts an existing one via `ExtractPod(livePod, \"my-controller\")`.\n2. `client-go/util/apply.NewRequest` marshals it to JSON (or CBOR if the feature gate is on) and sets `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`. (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/apply/apply.go:34-48`)\n3. The typed client (`kubernetes.Clientset`) issues a `PATCH` to the resource endpoint.\n\n### 3.2 API server: request routing\n\nIn `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`, `PatchResource` receives all PATCH requests. It reads the `Content-Type` header and dispatches:\n\n- `application/apply-patch+yaml` (or `+cbor`) \u2192 constructs an `applyPatcher` (`patch.go:488-498`)\n- `application/json-patch+json`, `application/merge-patch+json`, `application/strategic-merge-patch+json` \u2192 constructs a `jsonPatcher`\n\nThe outer `patcher` calls `rest.GuaranteedUpdate` (the storage-layer optimistic-concurrency loop), which in turn calls back `p.applyPatch` on each retry.\n\n### 3.3 Apply path (`applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject`, `patch.go:500-530`)\n\n```\napplyPatchToCurrentObject(ctx, currentObject)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 unmarshal patch bytes \u2192 *unstructured.Unstructured (patchObj)\n  \u2514\u2500 fieldManager.Apply(currentObject, patchObj, options.FieldManager, force)\n       \u2502\n       \u2554\u2550 FieldManager.Apply (internal/fieldmanager.go:183-208) \u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2557\n       \u2551  1. DecodeManagedFields(liveObj.managedFields)                   \u2551\n       \u2551  2. manager chain.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, managed, mgr, force)\u2551\n       \u2551  3. EncodeObjectManagedFields(resultObj, newManaged)             \u2551\n       \u255a\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u255d\n```\n\nInside the chain, `structuredMergeManager.Apply` (`internal/structuredmerge.go:121-182`) performs the actual merge:\n\n```\n1. Validate patchObj.GVK == groupVersion\n2. Validate patchObj.managedFields == nil\n3. Convert liveObj \u2192 versioned \u2192 typed (liveObjTyped)\n4. Convert patchObj \u2192 typed (patchObjTyped) \u2014 rejects duplicates\n5. merge.Updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion,\n                       managed.Fields(), manager, force)\n   \u2192 returns (newObjTyped, newManagedFields, err)\n6. Convert newObjTyped \u2192 unstructured \u2192 versioned\n7. Apply defaults (objectDefaulter.Default)\n8. Convert back to hub (unversioned) version\n```\n\nThe `merge.Updater` in SMD does the real work: it walks both typed values field by field, transfers ownership, and detects conflicts (fields in `patchObj` that are already owned by a different manager with a different value). Conflicts are returned as `merge.Conflicts`.\n\n### 3.4 Conflict surfacing (`internal/conflict.go`)\n\n`NewConflictError(conflicts)` converts `merge.Conflicts` into a `*errors.StatusError` (HTTP 409) with:\n\n- One `StatusCause` per conflicting field, type `CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict`.\n- `Field` set to the field path string.\n- `Message` naming the conflicting manager, its operation, API version, and timestamp.\n\nThe error message groups conflicts by manager and sorts deterministically (`conflict.go:50-70`).\n\n### 3.5 Update path (non-SSA writes)\n\nFor `PUT` and non-SSA `PATCH`, `FieldManager.Update` is called instead. The flow is:\n\n1. Decode managed fields from whichever object is more complete (live or new, preferring live for subresources).\n2. Strip `managedFields` from `newObj` so it is not tracked recursively.\n3. Call `manager chain.Update(liveObj, newObj, managed, manager)`.\n4. Inside `structuredMergeManager.Update`: convert both objects to SMD typed values, call `merge.Updater.Update` which simply computes the new ownership without merging content, return `newObj` unchanged but with updated managed fields.\n\n### 3.6 Noop-timestamp optimisation\n\n`IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer` (`apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/equality.go:114-226`) is a storage transformer that runs after the merge. When:\n\n- The number of managed field entries is unchanged, **and**\n- The managed fields are equal modulo timestamps, **and**\n- The rest of the object is semantically equal\n\n\u2026the transformer resets the updated timestamps back to their old values. This prevents SSA from bumping `resourceVersion` every time a controller reconciles without actually changing any field value.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Conflict errors (HTTP 409)\n\nThe most common SSA-specific failure. Causes:\n\n- Field already owned by a different manager (e.g., a human `kubectl apply` manager and a controller both trying to set `spec.replicas`).\n- Resolution: use `--force-conflicts` / `force=true`, or coordinate by removing the field from one actor's apply configuration.\n\n### 4.2 Version mismatch (HTTP 400)\n\n`VersionCheckManager` rejects an apply whose `apiVersion` does not match the request scope. This happens when a client sends a v1beta1 object to a `/v1` endpoint or vice versa.\n\n### 4.3 Manager entry cap\n\n`CapManagersManager` hard-caps update-type managers at `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:35`). When exceeded, the oldest entries are merged into synthetic `ancient-changes` buckets keyed by API version. The merge is a union of the field sets, so no field ownership is lost, but attribution to the original manager is. This is relevant in clusters with many short-lived controllers or CI systems that use unique manager names per run.\n\n### 4.4 CRD without structural schema\n\n`NewDeducedTypeConverter` treats all lists as atomic. This means list items are compared by their full value, not by a merge key. A controller that appends to a list in a schema-free CRD will conflict with any other writer of that list. This is correct behaviour but surprises operators.\n\n### 4.5 `before-first-apply` synthetic entry\n\nWhen SSA is used for the first time on an object that was previously managed purely by updates, `ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager` synthesises a `before-first-apply` manager entry representing the existing live state. This prevents the apply from incorrectly claiming that every field in the live object is a conflict. The entry is removed once the applier's managed fields replace it.\n\n### 4.6 `UpdateNoErrors` behaviour\n\n`FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:145-163`) silently drops managed fields on error and rate-limits error logging to once per second. This is intentional: a failure to update managed fields must never block the actual object write. The trade-off is silent data loss of managed-field bookkeeping, which can cause spurious conflicts on the next apply.\n\n### 4.7 Mutating admission and managed fields\n\nMutating admission webhooks can observe and modify `metadata.managedFields` in the object passed to them. The `managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` (`apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`) wraps the admission chain: if admission mutates managed fields into an invalid state (e.g., missing `fieldsType`), the controller resets them to their pre-admission state and emits a warning to the client. This prevents corrupt managed fields from reaching etcd.\n\n### 4.8 Subresource isolation\n\nSSA tracks per-subresource ownership. The `subresource` field in the manager identifier distinguishes, for example, `status` writes from `spec` writes. The `ScaleHandler` (`managedfields/scalehandler.go`) performs path remapping when a `scale` subresource is read or written: the `spec.replicas` path in the main resource is mapped to `spec.replicas` in the `autoscaling/v1` scale object so ownership is preserved across the subresource boundary.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customisation Hooks\n\n### 5.1 `TypeConverter` replacement\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` accept any `TypeConverter`. Callers can inject a custom converter by constructing the chain manually via `internal.NewStructuredMergeManager` and `internal.NewDefaultFieldManager`. The `schemeTypeConverter` (2025 addition) provides a runtime-Scheme-based path that avoids the OpenAPI map construction for contexts where the scheme is already available.\n\n### 5.2 `resetFields` filter\n\nBoth `NewStructuredMergeManager` and `NewCRDStructuredMergeManager` accept a `map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter` parameter (`resetFields`). This is passed directly to `merge.Updater.IgnoreFilter`. Any field matching the filter is excluded from managed-field tracking for all operations. This is used to exclude status subresource fields from spec applies (the controller manager uses it for `spec`/`status` isolation).\n\n### 5.3 Custom `Manager` wrappers\n\nBecause the chain is constructed from composable `Manager` wrappers, operators of embedded API servers can insert their own layer between any two existing ones. The `Manager` interface requires only `Update` and `Apply`, so a layer can be a pass-through for one operation and perform custom logic for the other.\n\n### 5.4 `ForKind` and the extract-modify-apply pattern\n\n`applyconfigurations.ForKind(gvk)` returns a zero-value `*ApplyConfiguration` for any registered GVK. This is used by generic server-side code (e.g., field-validation test harnesses) that does not know the concrete type at compile time.\n\n`Extract*` functions (e.g., `ExtractPod`, `ExtractPodFrom`) delegate to `managedfields.ExtractInto` which uses `ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` from SMD to project only the fields owned by the named manager onto an empty value. This is the standard pattern for controllers that need to reconcile without stealing ownership from other managers:\n\n```go\n// Retrieve the current state\npod, _ := client.CoreV1().Pods(ns).Get(ctx, name, metav1.GetOptions{})\n// Extract only the fields owned by this controller\ncfg, _ := corev1apply.ExtractPod(pod, \"my-controller\")\n// Mutate the fields this controller cares about\ncfg.WithLabels(map[string]string{\"app\": \"my-app\"})\n// Apply\nclient.CoreV1().Pods(ns).Apply(ctx, cfg, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"my-controller\"})\n```\n\n### 5.5 Risks of force-apply\n\n`force=true` silently takes ownership of any conflicting field from any other manager. If used carelessly, it permanently removes attribution from other managers. For subresource status, this can produce feedback loops where controllers repeatedly steal ownership from each other, bumping `resourceVersion` on every reconciliation.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance: TypeConverter construction cost\n\n`NewTypeConverter` (`internal/typeconverter.go:45-54`) calls `schemaconv.ToSchemaFromOpenAPI` which walks the full OpenAPI model. This is a one-time startup cost per GVK set (constructed once per `RequestScope` in the API server). The resulting `parser` map is shared across all requests for a given GVK. For clusters with large numbers of CRD schemas this can be a significant startup memory cost; each schema is kept alive for the lifetime of the server process.\n\n### 6.2 Performance: noop-timestamp suppression\n\nWithout the `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer`, every SSA reconciliation by a controller increments `resourceVersion` even when no data changes. This causes unnecessary watch events, etcd writes, and informer cache invalidation across the cluster. The transformer does two object comparisons on the hot path; the fast path (`eqFn(oldManagedFields, newManagedFields)`) is cheap but the slow path (full object equality) can be expensive for large objects. It is enabled by default but can be disabled by setting `KUBE_APISERVER_AVOID_NOOP_SSA_TIMESTAMP_UPDATES=false`.\n\n### 6.3 Performance: manager entry accumulation\n\nEach unique manager name used in an `Update` creates a new entry in `metadata.managedFields`. If CI pipelines or operator frameworks generate unique names per invocation (e.g., job ID, timestamp), `CapManagersManager` will start merging entries after 10 are accumulated. The merge is a union, so no ownership is lost, but the resulting `ancient-changes` entries make it impossible to tell which specific run set which field. Stable manager names are strongly recommended.\n\n### 6.4 Reliability: `UpdateNoErrors` silent degradation\n\nController authors should be aware that `UpdateNoErrors` never returns an error. A bug in managed-field encoding will silently produce objects with empty `managedFields`. Those objects will be treated by subsequent SSA applies as having no prior ownership (`before-first-apply` bootstrap), potentially causing unexpected conflict errors or field ownership gaps that are difficult to debug.\n\n### 6.5 Maintainability: code generation\n\nThe `applyconfigurations` package is entirely generated by `applyconfiguration-gen` (invoked via `hack/update-codegen.sh`). Extending an API type requires re-running the generator; hand-editing generated files will be overwritten. The `ForKind` function in `utils.go` must be regenerated whenever a new kind is added or a version is promoted.\n\n### 6.6 Wire encoding and CBOR\n\nAs of recent Kubernetes versions, the feature gates `ClientsAllowCBOR` and `ClientsPreferCBOR` can switch the wire format from JSON/YAML to CBOR for both the apply patch body and the SSA Content-Type header (`apply.go:38-41`, `customresource_handler.go:332-334`). The server-side handling is symmetric: supported `Content-Type` values are extended at registration time. This is a performance and binary-compactness improvement with no semantic change.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\nThe following locations are the primary sources for understanding this subsystem:\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/\n  fieldmanager.go              Public facade; NewDefaultFieldManager / NewDefaultCRDFieldManager\n  extract.go                   ExtractInto \u2014 reconstruct apply config from live object\n  gvkparser.go                 GvkParser \u2014 maps GVKs to SMD ParseableTypes from OpenAPI proto.Models\n  scalehandler.go              ScaleHandler \u2014 path remapping for scale subresource\n  typeconverter.go             TypeConverter interface (re-exported from internal)\n\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/\n  manager.go                   Manager interface definition\n  fieldmanager.go              FieldManager struct; Apply, Update, UpdateNoErrors; NewDefaultFieldManager chain\n  structuredmerge.go           structuredMergeManager; calls merge.Updater (SMD)\n  typeconverter.go             typeConverter (OpenAPI-backed), deducedTypeConverter (CRD schema-free)\n  runtimetypeconverter.go      schemeTypeConverter (runtime.Scheme-backed, 2025 addition)\n  versionconverter.go          versionConverter \u2014 bridges SMD's merge.Converter to k8s ObjectConvertor\n  managedfields.go             Encode/Decode ManagedFields; BuildManagerIdentifier\n  conflict.go                  NewConflictError \u2014 formats 409 responses\n  stripmeta.go                 StripMetaManager \u2014 removes synthetic paths from field sets\n  managedfieldsupdater.go      ManagedFieldsUpdater \u2014 change detection, timestamp stamping\n  buildmanagerinfo.go          BuildManagerInfoManager \u2014 JSON manager identifier construction\n  capmanagers.go               CapManagersManager \u2014 caps update-manager entry count at 10\n  skipnonapplied.go            ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager; before-first-apply bootstrap\n  lastappliedmanager.go        LastAppliedManager \u2014 CSA\u2192SSA migration for kubectl\n  lastappliedupdater.go        LastAppliedUpdater \u2014 keeps CSA annotation in sync\n  versioncheck.go              VersionCheckManager \u2014 rejects mismatched apiVersion on apply\n\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/\n  patch.go                     PatchResource HTTP handler; applyPatcher; patcher; GuaranteedUpdate loop\n  fieldmanager/\n    admission.go               managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController \u2014 protect managedFields from bad webhooks\n    equality.go                IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer \u2014 noop-timestamp suppression\n\nstaging/src/k8s.io/client-go/\n  applyconfigurations/\n    core/v1/pod.go             Example generated apply configuration; Pod(), ExtractPod()\n    meta/v1/objectmeta.go      ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration \u2014 pointer-field metadata builder\n    internal/internal.go       Embedded OpenAPI schema used by Extract* functions\n    utils.go                   ForKind \u2014 dispatch from GVK to zero-value ApplyConfiguration\n  util/apply/apply.go          NewRequest \u2014 marshal + Content-Type for SSA HTTP requests\n```\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"
}
Output
{
  "content": "# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and ApplyConfigurations: A Deep Guide\n\n## 1. Purpose and Boundaries\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative ownership protocol built into the Kubernetes API server. Where the older `kubectl apply` (client-side apply) computed a three-way diff on the client and then submitted a strategic-merge patch, SSA moves the merge logic entirely to the server. The server becomes the single source of truth about which actor controls each field of a resource, and conflicts between actors are surfaced as hard errors rather than silently clobbered.\n\nThe system has two main purposes:\n\n1. **Field ownership tracking** \u2013 every field in a resource's live state is attributed to the last manager that set it, stored in `metadata.managedFields`.\n2. **Controlled merge** \u2013 when a new apply is received the server merges the incoming \"desired intent\" with the live state under explicit conflict semantics: unknown fields that the caller does not touch are left alone; fields the caller explicitly declares ownership of that are already owned by a different manager produce a `409 Conflict` unless `force=true` is passed.\n\n### Upstream / downstream dependencies\n\n| Layer | What it provides |\n|---|---|\n| `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` (SMD) | Schema-aware value comparison, field-path representations, `merge.Updater` (the merge engine) |\n| `k8s.io/kube-openapi` | Converts OpenAPI v2 models into SMD schema types |\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields` | Public facade: `FieldManager`, `TypeConverter`, `ExtractInto`, `ScaleHandler`, `GvkParser` |\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal` | All business logic: the layered `Manager` chain, encoding/decoding, conflict formatting |\n| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers` | HTTP `PATCH` handler that selects SSA when `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml` (or `+cbor`) |\n| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager` | Admission controller wrapper (`managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController`), noop-timestamp optimization |\n| `k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations` | Code-generated, type-safe Go builders (one per API kind/version) for constructing apply payloads |\n| `k8s.io/client-go/util/apply` | Thin helper that marshals an apply configuration and sets the right `Content-Type` header |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 The `Manager` interface\n\n```\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/manager.go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n    Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, fieldManager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n}\n```\n\n`Manager` is the central abstraction. Every behavioural concern is implemented as a separate `Manager` wrapper that decorates an inner `Manager`. The production chain is assembled in `NewDefaultFieldManager` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:57-75`) as a nested sequence of constructors, innermost first:\n\n```\nVersionCheckManager\n  \u2514\u2500 LastAppliedUpdater\n       \u2514\u2500 LastAppliedManager\n            \u2514\u2500 ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager\n                 \u2514\u2500 CapManagersManager\n                      \u2514\u2500 BuildManagerInfoManager\n                           \u2514\u2500 ManagedFieldsUpdater\n                                \u2514\u2500 StripMetaManager\n                                     \u2514\u2500 structuredMergeManager   \u2190 SMD engine\n```\n\nEach layer has a single, narrow job:\n\n| Layer | File | Job |\n|---|---|---|\n| `structuredMergeManager` | `internal/structuredmerge.go` | Calls `merge.Updater.Update` / `.Apply`; owns all object-to-typed and typed-to-object conversions; applies defaults after a successful apply |\n| `StripMetaManager` | `internal/stripmeta.go` | Removes synthetic paths (`apiVersion`, `kind`, `metadata.name`, `metadata.managedFields`, \u2026) from the resulting field set so they are never tracked as owned |\n| `ManagedFieldsUpdater` | `internal/managedfieldsupdater.go` | For updates: detects whether any fields actually changed (by using a sentinel manager name `current-operation`) and, if so, merges them into the real manager entry and stamps the current time. For applies: stamps the operation time |\n| `BuildManagerInfoManager` | `internal/buildmanagerinfo.go` | Serialises the manager identifier: for updates it encodes `{manager, operation, apiVersion, subresource}` as JSON; for applies it omits `apiVersion` so a manager is always the same identity across versions |\n| `CapManagersManager` | `internal/capmanagers.go` | Caps the number of update-type manager entries at `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers` (10) by merging the oldest entries into per-version `ancient-changes` buckets |\n| `ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager` | `internal/skipnonapplied.go` | For objects with no managed fields, skips tracking on updates; for applies, synthesises an `Update` for the live object under the name `before-first-apply` so that the first apply has something to merge against |\n| `LastAppliedManager` | `internal/lastappliedmanager.go` | Intercepts `kubectl` applies and, if there are conflicts, checks whether the conflicting fields were previously owned by the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation; if so, auto-forces those specific fields (CSA\u2192SSA migration) |\n| `LastAppliedUpdater` | `internal/lastappliedupdater.go` | After a successful `kubectl` apply, keeps the `last-applied-configuration` annotation in sync with the new configuration (backward compatibility) |\n| `VersionCheckManager` | `internal/versioncheck.go` | Rejects applies whose `apiVersion/kind` do not match the request scope's GVK |\n\n### 2.2 `FieldManager` (public facade)\n\n`internal.FieldManager` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:45-48`) is not another `Manager` implementor in the chain; it is the outermost struct that callers interact with directly. It owns two responsibilities:\n\n1. Decoding the wire-format `metadata.managedFields` slice from `metav1.ManagedFieldsEntry` into the SMD-internal `fieldpath.ManagedFields` representation (`DecodeManagedFields`).\n2. Re-encoding the result back into `metadata.managedFields` after a successful operation (`EncodeObjectManagedFields`).\n\nThe public package exposes only a type alias (`type FieldManager = internal.FieldManager`) at `managedfields/fieldmanager.go:32` and two constructors:\n\n- `NewDefaultFieldManager` \u2013 for built-in typed API resources; requires a non-nil `TypeConverter` derived from the OpenAPI model.\n- `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` \u2013 for CRDs; uses `deducedTypeConverter` which treats all lists as atomic (no structural schema required).\n\n### 2.3 `TypeConverter`\n\n```\n// internal/typeconverter.go:34-37\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    ObjectToTyped(runtime.Object, ...typed.ValidationOptions) (*typed.TypedValue, error)\n    TypedToObject(*typed.TypedValue) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\nTwo implementations:\n\n- `typeConverter` (`internal/typeconverter.go:39-43`) \u2013 OpenAPI-backed; maps each GVK to a `*typed.ParseableType` built from `schemaconv.ToSchemaFromOpenAPI`. For unstructured objects it calls `t.FromUnstructured`; for structured it calls `t.FromStructured`.\n- `deducedTypeConverter` (`internal/typeconverter.go:75-100`) \u2013 schema-free; uses `typed.DeducedParseableType` which treats all lists atomically. Used for CRDs without structural schemas.\n- `schemeTypeConverter` (`internal/runtimetypeconverter.go`) \u2013 runtime-Scheme-backed; looks up the OpenAPI definition name from the Scheme (`scheme.ToOpenAPIDefinitionName`), then delegates to the parser. Introduced in 2025 as an alternative to the OpenAPI-map-based approach.\n\n### 2.4 `Managed` / `ManagedInterface`\n\n`fieldpath.ManagedFields` (from SMD) maps a JSON-encoded manager identifier string to a `fieldpath.VersionedSet` (a field set tagged with its API version and an `Applied` flag). The Kubernetes layer wraps this with timestamps in `managedStruct` implementing `ManagedInterface` (also aliased as `Managed`).\n\nManager identifiers are JSON-encoded `metav1.ManagedFieldsEntry` structs with `FieldsType`, `FieldsV1`, and `Time` zeroed out (see `BuildManagerIdentifier`, `internal/managedfields.go:134-158`). For applies, `APIVersion` is also omitted, making the identifier stable across version upgrades.\n\n### 2.5 ApplyConfiguration builders (client-go)\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` contains one auto-generated Go file per API type (e.g., `core/v1/pod.go`). Each file defines:\n\n- A `*ApplyConfiguration` struct with all fields as pointers (absent = not set, present = intent to set/own).\n- `With*` fluent builder methods for every field.\n- A `ForKind(gvk)` dispatch function in `utils.go` (1920-line generated file) that returns the correct zero-value `*ApplyConfiguration`.\n- `Extract*From` functions that call `managedfields.ExtractInto` to reconstruct the apply configuration from an existing live object's managed-fields entry \u2014 enabling the extract-modify-apply pattern.\n\n`ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration` (`meta/v1/objectmeta.go`) is the metadata half; it uses pointer fields to distinguish \"set this field\" from \"don't touch this field\", mirroring the JSON `omitempty` semantics that drive the SMD merge.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Client side\n\n1. The caller builds an `*ApplyConfiguration` (e.g., `corev1.Pod(\"my-pod\", \"default\").WithSpec(...)`) or extracts an existing one via `ExtractPod(livePod, \"my-controller\")`.\n2. `client-go/util/apply.NewRequest` marshals it to JSON (or CBOR if the feature gate is on) and sets `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`. (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/apply/apply.go:34-48`)\n3. The typed client (`kubernetes.Clientset`) issues a `PATCH` to the resource endpoint.\n\n### 3.2 API server: request routing\n\nIn `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`, `PatchResource` receives all PATCH requests. It reads the `Content-Type` header and dispatches:\n\n- `application/apply-patch+yaml` (or `+cbor`) \u2192 constructs an `applyPatcher` (`patch.go:488-498`)\n- `application/json-patch+json`, `application/merge-patch+json`, `application/strategic-merge-patch+json` \u2192 constructs a `jsonPatcher`\n\nThe outer `patcher` calls `rest.GuaranteedUpdate` (the storage-layer optimistic-concurrency loop), which in turn calls back `p.applyPatch` on each retry.\n\n### 3.3 Apply path (`applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject`, `patch.go:500-530`)\n\n```\napplyPatchToCurrentObject(ctx, currentObject)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 unmarshal patch bytes \u2192 *unstructured.Unstructured (patchObj)\n  \u2514\u2500 fieldManager.Apply(currentObject, patchObj, options.FieldManager, force)\n       \u2502\n       \u2554\u2550 FieldManager.Apply (internal/fieldmanager.go:183-208) \u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2557\n       \u2551  1. DecodeManagedFields(liveObj.managedFields)                   \u2551\n       \u2551  2. manager chain.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, managed, mgr, force)\u2551\n       \u2551  3. EncodeObjectManagedFields(resultObj, newManaged)             \u2551\n       \u255a\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u2550\u255d\n```\n\nInside the chain, `structuredMergeManager.Apply` (`internal/structuredmerge.go:121-182`) performs the actual merge:\n\n```\n1. Validate patchObj.GVK == groupVersion\n2. Validate patchObj.managedFields == nil\n3. Convert liveObj \u2192 versioned \u2192 typed (liveObjTyped)\n4. Convert patchObj \u2192 typed (patchObjTyped) \u2014 rejects duplicates\n5. merge.Updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion,\n                       managed.Fields(), manager, force)\n   \u2192 returns (newObjTyped, newManagedFields, err)\n6. Convert newObjTyped \u2192 unstructured \u2192 versioned\n7. Apply defaults (objectDefaulter.Default)\n8. Convert back to hub (unversioned) version\n```\n\nThe `merge.Updater` in SMD does the real work: it walks both typed values field by field, transfers ownership, and detects conflicts (fields in `patchObj` that are already owned by a different manager with a different value). Conflicts are returned as `merge.Conflicts`.\n\n### 3.4 Conflict surfacing (`internal/conflict.go`)\n\n`NewConflictError(conflicts)` converts `merge.Conflicts` into a `*errors.StatusError` (HTTP 409) with:\n\n- One `StatusCause` per conflicting field, type `CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict`.\n- `Field` set to the field path string.\n- `Message` naming the conflicting manager, its operation, API version, and timestamp.\n\nThe error message groups conflicts by manager and sorts deterministically (`conflict.go:50-70`).\n\n### 3.5 Update path (non-SSA writes)\n\nFor `PUT` and non-SSA `PATCH`, `FieldManager.Update` is called instead. The flow is:\n\n1. Decode managed fields from whichever object is more complete (live or new, preferring live for subresources).\n2. Strip `managedFields` from `newObj` so it is not tracked recursively.\n3. Call `manager chain.Update(liveObj, newObj, managed, manager)`.\n4. Inside `structuredMergeManager.Update`: convert both objects to SMD typed values, call `merge.Updater.Update` which simply computes the new ownership without merging content, return `newObj` unchanged but with updated managed fields.\n\n### 3.6 Noop-timestamp optimisation\n\n`IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer` (`apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/equality.go:114-226`) is a storage transformer that runs after the merge. When:\n\n- The number of managed field entries is unchanged, **and**\n- The managed fields are equal modulo timestamps, **and**\n- The rest of the object is semantically equal\n\n\u2026the transformer resets the updated timestamps back to their old values. This prevents SSA from bumping `resourceVersion` every time a controller reconciles without actually changing any field value.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Conflict errors (HTTP 409)\n\nThe most common SSA-specific failure. Causes:\n\n- Field already owned by a different manager (e.g., a human `kubectl apply` manager and a controller both trying to set `spec.replicas`).\n- Resolution: use `--force-conflicts` / `force=true`, or coordinate by removing the field from one actor's apply configuration.\n\n### 4.2 Version mismatch (HTTP 400)\n\n`VersionCheckManager` rejects an apply whose `apiVersion` does not match the request scope. This happens when a client sends a v1beta1 object to a `/v1` endpoint or vice versa.\n\n### 4.3 Manager entry cap\n\n`CapManagersManager` hard-caps update-type managers at `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:35`). When exceeded, the oldest entries are merged into synthetic `ancient-changes` buckets keyed by API version. The merge is a union of the field sets, so no field ownership is lost, but attribution to the original manager is. This is relevant in clusters with many short-lived controllers or CI systems that use unique manager names per run.\n\n### 4.4 CRD without structural schema\n\n`NewDeducedTypeConverter` treats all lists as atomic. This means list items are compared by their full value, not by a merge key. A controller that appends to a list in a schema-free CRD will conflict with any other writer of that list. This is correct behaviour but surprises operators.\n\n### 4.5 `before-first-apply` synthetic entry\n\nWhen SSA is used for the first time on an object that was previously managed purely by updates, `ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager` synthesises a `before-first-apply` manager entry representing the existing live state. This prevents the apply from incorrectly claiming that every field in the live object is a conflict. The entry is removed once the applier's managed fields replace it.\n\n### 4.6 `UpdateNoErrors` behaviour\n\n`FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:145-163`) silently drops managed fields on error and rate-limits error logging to once per second. This is intentional: a failure to update managed fields must never block the actual object write. The trade-off is silent data loss of managed-field bookkeeping, which can cause spurious conflicts on the next apply.\n\n### 4.7 Mutating admission and managed fields\n\nMutating admission webhooks can observe and modify `metadata.managedFields` in the object passed to them. The `managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` (`apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`) wraps the admission chain: if admission mutates managed fields into an invalid state (e.g., missing `fieldsType`), the controller resets them to their pre-admission state and emits a warning to the client. This prevents corrupt managed fields from reaching etcd.\n\n### 4.8 Subresource isolation\n\nSSA tracks per-subresource ownership. The `subresource` field in the manager identifier distinguishes, for example, `status` writes from `spec` writes. The `ScaleHandler` (`managedfields/scalehandler.go`) performs path remapping when a `scale` subresource is read or written: the `spec.replicas` path in the main resource is mapped to `spec.replicas` in the `autoscaling/v1` scale object so ownership is preserved across the subresource boundary.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customisation Hooks\n\n### 5.1 `TypeConverter` replacement\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` accept any `TypeConverter`. Callers can inject a custom converter by constructing the chain manually via `internal.NewStructuredMergeManager` and `internal.NewDefaultFieldManager`. The `schemeTypeConverter` (2025 addition) provides a runtime-Scheme-based path that avoids the OpenAPI map construction for contexts where the scheme is already available.\n\n### 5.2 `resetFields` filter\n\nBoth `NewStructuredMergeManager` and `NewCRDStructuredMergeManager` accept a `map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter` parameter (`resetFields`). This is passed directly to `merge.Updater.IgnoreFilter`. Any field matching the filter is excluded from managed-field tracking for all operations. This is used to exclude status subresource fields from spec applies (the controller manager uses it for `spec`/`status` isolation).\n\n### 5.3 Custom `Manager` wrappers\n\nBecause the chain is constructed from composable `Manager` wrappers, operators of embedded API servers can insert their own layer between any two existing ones. The `Manager` interface requires only `Update` and `Apply`, so a layer can be a pass-through for one operation and perform custom logic for the other.\n\n### 5.4 `ForKind` and the extract-modify-apply pattern\n\n`applyconfigurations.ForKind(gvk)` returns a zero-value `*ApplyConfiguration` for any registered GVK. This is used by generic server-side code (e.g., field-validation test harnesses) that does not know the concrete type at compile time.\n\n`Extract*` functions (e.g., `ExtractPod`, `ExtractPodFrom`) delegate to `managedfields.ExtractInto` which uses `ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` from SMD to project only the fields owned by the named manager onto an empty value. This is the standard pattern for controllers that need to reconcile without stealing ownership from other managers:\n\n```go\n// Retrieve the current state\npod, _ := client.CoreV1().Pods(ns).Get(ctx, name, metav1.GetOptions{})\n// Extract only the fields owned by this controller\ncfg, _ := corev1apply.ExtractPod(pod, \"my-controller\")\n// Mutate the fields this controller cares about\ncfg.WithLabels(map[string]string{\"app\": \"my-app\"})\n// Apply\nclient.CoreV1().Pods(ns).Apply(ctx, cfg, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"my-controller\"})\n```\n\n### 5.5 Risks of force-apply\n\n`force=true` silently takes ownership of any conflicting field from any other manager. If used carelessly, it permanently removes attribution from other managers. For subresource status, this can produce feedback loops where controllers repeatedly steal ownership from each other, bumping `resourceVersion` on every reconciliation.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance: TypeConverter construction cost\n\n`NewTypeConverter` (`internal/typeconverter.go:45-54`) calls `schemaconv.ToSchemaFromOpenAPI` which walks the full OpenAPI model. This is a one-time startup cost per GVK set (constructed once per `RequestScope` in the API server). The resulting `parser` map is shared across all requests for a given GVK. For clusters with large numbers of CRD schemas this can be a significant startup memory cost; each schema is kept alive for the lifetime of the server process.\n\n### 6.2 Performance: noop-timestamp suppression\n\nWithout the `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer`, every SSA reconciliation by a controller increments `resourceVersion` even when no data changes. This causes unnecessary watch events, etcd writes, and informer cache invalidation across the cluster. The transformer does two object comparisons on the hot path; the fast path (`eqFn(oldManagedFields, newManagedFields)`) is cheap but the slow path (full object equality) can be expensive for large objects. It is enabled by default but can be disabled by setting `KUBE_APISERVER_AVOID_NOOP_SSA_TIMESTAMP_UPDATES=false`.\n\n### 6.3 Performance: manager entry accumulation\n\nEach unique manager name used in an `Update` creates a new entry in `metadata.managedFields`. If CI pipelines or operator frameworks generate unique names per invocation (e.g., job ID, timestamp), `CapManagersManager` will start merging entries after 10 are accumulated. The merge is a union, so no ownership is lost, but the resulting `ancient-changes` entries make it impossible to tell which specific run set which field. Stable manager names are strongly recommended.\n\n### 6.4 Reliability: `UpdateNoErrors` silent degradation\n\nController authors should be aware that `UpdateNoErrors` never returns an error. A bug in managed-field encoding will silently produce objects with empty `managedFields`. Those objects will be treated by subsequent SSA applies as having no prior ownership (`before-first-apply` bootstrap), potentially causing unexpected conflict errors or field ownership gaps that are difficult to debug.\n\n### 6.5 Maintainability: code generation\n\nThe `applyconfigurations` package is entirely generated by `applyconfiguration-gen` (invoked via `hack/update-codegen.sh`). Extending an API type requires re-running the generator; hand-editing generated files will be overwritten. The `ForKind` function in `utils.go` must be regenerated whenever a new kind is added or a version is promoted.\n\n### 6.6 Wire encoding and CBOR\n\nAs of recent Kubernetes versions, the feature gates `ClientsAllowCBOR` and `ClientsPreferCBOR` can switch the wire format from JSON/YAML to CBOR for both the apply patch body and the SSA Content-Type header (`apply.go:38-41`, `customresource_handler.go:332-334`). The server-side handling is symmetric: supported `Content-Type` values are extended at registration time. This is a performance and binary-compactness improvement with no semantic change.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\nThe following locations are the primary sources for understanding this subsystem:\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/\n  fieldmanager.go              Public facade; # Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and ApplyConfigurations: A Deep Guide

## 1. Purpose and Boundaries

Server-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative ownership protocol built into the Kubernetes API server. Where the older `kubectl apply` (client-side apply) computed a three-way diff on the client and then submitted a strategic-merge patch, SSA moves the merge logic entirely to the server. The server becomes the single source of truth about which actor controls each field of a resource, and conflicts between actors are surfaced as hard errors rather than silently clobbered.

The system has two main purposes:

1. **Field ownership tracking** – every field in a resource's live state is attributed to the last manager that set it, stored in `metadata.managedFields`.
2. **Controlled merge** – when a new apply is received the server merges the incoming "desired intent" with the live state under explicit conflict semantics: unknown fields that the caller does not touch are left alone; fields the caller explicitly declares ownership of that are already owned by a different manager produce a `409 Conflict` unless `force=true` is passed.

### Upstream / downstream dependencies

| Layer | What it provides |
|---|---|
| `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` (SMD) | Schema-aware value comparison, field-path representations, `merge.Updater` (the merge engine) |
| `k8s.io/kube-openapi` | Converts OpenAPI v2 models into SMD schema types |
| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields` | Public facade: `FieldManager`, `TypeConverter`, `ExtractInto`, `ScaleHandler`, `GvkParser` |
| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal` | All business logic: the layered `Manager` chain, encoding/decoding, conflict formatting |
| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers` | HTTP `PATCH` handler that se
... (truncated)
